		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Portuguese footballer</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">


</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other people named Bruno Fernandes, see <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Fernandes_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Bruno Fernandes (disambiguation)">Bruno Fernandes (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This name uses <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_name" title="Portuguese name">Portuguese naming customs</a>: the first or maternal <a href="/wiki/Surname" title="Surname">family name</a> is <i>Borges</i>&#32;and the second or paternal family name is <i>Fernandes</i>.</div>

<p><b>Bruno Miguel Borges Fernandes</b> (<span style="font-size:85%;">European Portuguese:&#160;</span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">[bunu fnd]</a></span>; born 8 September 1994) is a Portuguese professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">midfielder</a> for <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal national team</a>.
</p><p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Maia,_Portugal" title="Maia, Portugal">Maia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Area_of_Porto" class="mw-redirect" title="Metropolitan Area of Porto">Porto</a>, Fernandes started his career at Italian <a href="/wiki/Serie_B" title="Serie B">Serie B</a> side <a href="/wiki/Novara_Calcio" title="Novara Calcio">Novara</a> but soon made a move to <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> side <a href="/wiki/Udinese_Calcio" title="Udinese Calcio">Udinese</a> in 2013, followed by <a href="/wiki/U.C._Sampdoria" title="U.C. Sampdoria">Sampdoria</a> three years later. After five years in Italy, he signed with <a href="/wiki/Sporting_CP" title="Sporting CP">Sporting CP</a> in 2017, where he was named club captain. He won back-to-back <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%A7a_da_Liga" title="Taça da Liga">Taças da Liga</a> in <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Ta%C3%A7a_da_Liga" title="2017–18 Taça da Liga">2018</a> and <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_Ta%C3%A7a_da_Liga" title="2018–19 Taça da Liga">2019</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%A7a_de_Portugal" title="Taça de Portugal">Taça de Portugal</a>, leading to him being named <a href="/wiki/LPFP_Primeira_Liga_Player_of_the_Year" title="LPFP Primeira Liga Player of the Year">Primeira Liga Player of the Year</a> in both seasons. In 2018–19, he scored a record of 33 goals in all competitions, making him the highest-scoring Portuguese midfielder and the highest-scoring midfielder in Europe in a single season. Fernandes' performances sparked the interest of several Premier League clubs, with Manchester United signing him for an initial €55&#160;million (£47&#160;million) in January 2020, becoming the second-highest fee for a Portuguese player leaving the domestic league.
</p><p>Fernandes made his senior debut for Portugal in November 2017, after previously being capped at <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_under-19_football_team" title="Portugal national under-19 football team">under-19</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_under-20_football_team" title="Portugal national under-20 football team">under-20</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_under-21_football_team" title="Portugal national under-21 football team">under-21</a> levels. He also represented Portugal at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament" title="Football at the 2016 Summer Olympics – Men&#39;s tournament">2016 Summer Olympics</a>. He was chosen in Portugal's squads for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 World Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Nations_League_Finals" title="2019 UEFA Nations League Finals">2019 UEFA Nations League Finals</a>, winning the latter and being named in the <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Nations_League_Finals#Awards" title="2019 UEFA Nations League Finals">Team of the Tournament</a>.
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Novara">Novara</span></h3>
<p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Maia,_Portugal" title="Maia, Portugal">Maia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Area_of_Porto" class="mw-redirect" title="Metropolitan Area of Porto">Metropolitan Area of Porto</a>, Fernandes played most of his youth football with local club <a href="/wiki/Boavista_F.C." title="Boavista F.C.">Boavista FC</a>. On 27 August 2012, he joined <a href="/wiki/Novara_Calcio" title="Novara Calcio">Novara Calcio</a> in Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After only a few weeks with the youth sides, Fernandes was promoted to the first team in <a href="/wiki/Serie_B" title="Serie B">Serie B</a>, and went on to appear in slightly more than half of the league games during the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Serie_B" title="2012–13 Serie B">2012–13 season</a>, helping his team to fifth place and the promotion play-offs.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Udinese">Udinese</span></h3>
<p>In summer 2013, Fernandes signed for <a href="/wiki/Udinese_Calcio" title="Udinese Calcio">Udinese Calcio</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Co-ownership_(football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Co-ownership (football)">co-ownership deal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> He made his debut in <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> on 3 November, coming on as a second-half <a href="/wiki/Substitute_(association_football)" title="Substitute (association football)">substitute</a> in a 0–3 home loss against <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Fernandes scored his first league goal on 7 December 2013, in a 3–3 draw at <a href="/wiki/S.S.C._Napoli" title="S.S.C. Napoli">S.S.C. Napoli</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> He scored again in the second match between the sides (a 1–1 draw).<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sampdoria">Sampdoria</span></h3>
<p>On 16 August 2016, Fernandes moved to <a href="/wiki/U.C._Sampdoria" title="U.C. Sampdoria">U.C. Sampdoria</a> on loan with an obligation to be signed permanently.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He made his league debut twelve days later, playing six minutes in a 2–1 home win over <a href="/wiki/Atalanta_B.C." title="Atalanta B.C.">Atalanta BC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Fernandes scored his first goal for his new team on 26 September 2016, in a 1–2 away loss to <a href="/wiki/Cagliari_Calcio" title="Cagliari Calcio">Cagliari Calcio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> He scored 5 goals in 33 Serie A appearances during <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Serie_A" title="2016–17 Serie A">the campaign</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Soccerway_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soccerway-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> helping them to finish in tenth position.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sporting_CP">Sporting CP</span></h3>
<p>On 27 June 2017, after returning from the <a href="/wiki/2017_UEFA_European_Under-21_Championship" title="2017 UEFA European Under-21 Championship">UEFA European Under-21 Championship</a>, Fernandes joined <a href="/wiki/Sporting_CP" title="Sporting CP">Sporting CP</a> on a five years deal, for a reported fee of €8.5&#160;million plus bonuses.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> He scored four goals in his first five <a href="/wiki/Primeira_Liga" title="Primeira Liga">Primeira Liga</a> games, including a brace in a 5–0 away win against <a href="/wiki/Vit%C3%B3ria_S.C." title="Vitória S.C.">Vitória de Guimarães</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Fernandes' first appearance in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> group stage was on 12 September, where he put the visitors 3–0 ahead in the 43rd minute of an eventual <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2017–18 UEFA Champions League">3–2 win</a> at <a href="/wiki/Olympiacos_F.C." title="Olympiacos F.C.">Olympiacos FC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> He finished his first season with 16 goals across all competitions, second only to <a href="/wiki/Bas_Dost" title="Bas Dost">Bas Dost</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 May 2018, Fernandes and several of his teammates, including coaches, were injured following an attack by around 50 Sporting supporters at the club's training ground after the team finished third in the league and missed out on Champions League qualification.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Despite the events, the team agreed to play in <a href="/wiki/2018_Ta%C3%A7a_de_Portugal_Final" title="2018 Taça de Portugal Final">the final</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%A7a_de_Portugal" title="Taça de Portugal">Taça de Portugal</a> scheduled for the following weekend,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> eventually losing to <a href="/wiki/C.D._Aves" title="C.D. Aves">C.D. Aves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Fernandes was named the <a href="/wiki/LPFP_Primeira_Liga_Player_of_the_Year" title="LPFP Primeira Liga Player of the Year">Primeira Liga Player of the Year</a> on 6 July.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Four days later he signed a new five-year contract with a €100&#160;million release clause,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> having turned back on his original decision to leave the <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_Jos%C3%A9_Alvalade" title="Estádio José Alvalade">Estádio José Alvalade</a> following the departure of club president <a href="/wiki/Bruno_de_Carvalho" title="Bruno de Carvalho">Bruno de Carvalho</a>, and being given an improved salary in the process.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Fernandes scored his 23rd competitive goal of the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_Sporting_CP_season" title="2018–19 Sporting CP season">2018–19 campaign</a> during a 3–1 home win against <a href="/wiki/Portimonense_S.C." title="Portimonense S.C.">Portimonense S.C.</a> on 3 March 2019, through a late <a href="/wiki/Penalty_kick_(association_football)" title="Penalty kick (association football)">penalty</a>, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Lu%C3%ADs_Alves_Ribeiro_Oliveira" class="mw-redirect" title="António Luís Alves Ribeiro Oliveira">António Oliveira</a>'s club record for goals by a midfielder in a season, set in <a href="/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_Primeira_Divis%C3%A3o" title="1981–82 Primeira Divisão">1981–82</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> On 5 May, he scored a <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a> in an 8–1 away rout of <a href="/wiki/Belenenses_SAD" title="Belenenses SAD">Belenenses SAD</a>, in the process becoming the highest-scoring Portuguese midfielder in a single season of all time, with 31 goals to his name.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> He scored his 33rd and final goal of the season on 25 May 2019, during Sporting's victory against <a href="/wiki/FC_Porto" title="FC Porto">FC Porto</a> in the Taça de Portugal final.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fdj_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fdj-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> He was named Primeira Liga Player of the Year for the second successive year for his performances in the 2018–19 season.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He scored seven goals in his first 10 appearances of the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Sporting_CP_season" title="2019–20 Sporting CP season">2019–20 season</a>, including a run of scoring in six consecutive appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> This made him the third Sporting player in the 21st century to score in six or more consecutive appearances for the club, after <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1rio_Jardel" title="Mário Jardel">Mário Jardel</a> and Bas Dost.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> On 28 November, he scored twice and assisted the other two goals in a 4–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV Eindhoven</a>, which guaranteed Sporting qualification to the knockout stages of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_United">Manchester United</span></h3>
<h4><span id="2019.E2.80.9320_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2019–20_season">2019–20 season</span></h4>
<p>On 29 January 2020, English club <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> confirmed they had reached an agreement with Sporting for the transfer of Fernandes for a fee reportedly worth up to €80&#160;million (£67.6&#160;million),<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> subject to the player passing a medical and agreeing personal terms.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The transfer was officially completed the following day, for an initial fee of around €55&#160;million (£47&#160;million),<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> plus up to €25&#160;million (£21&#160;million) in add-ons and 10% of the profits should United ever sell Fernandes.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Fernandes signed a five-and-a-half-year contract.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He made his debut on 1 February, playing the full 90 minutes of a goalless draw at home to <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wolverhampton Wanderers F.C.">Wolverhampton Wanderers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In Manchester United's 2–0 away win over <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> on 17 February, he provided an assist for the second goal, a header from <a href="/wiki/Harry_Maguire" title="Harry Maguire">Harry Maguire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Fernandes came on as a late substitute for Manchester United against <a href="/wiki/Club_Brugge_KV" title="Club Brugge KV">Club Brugge</a> in a 1–1 draw on his European debut for the club.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first goal for Manchester United against <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a> on 23 February, converting from the penalty spot in an eventual 3–0 victory at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a>, a match in which he also provided an assist for the third goal scored by <a href="/wiki/Mason_Greenwood" title="Mason Greenwood">Mason Greenwood</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> His first European goal for the club came in the second leg of their UEFA Europa League round of 32 tie against <a href="/wiki/Club_Brugge_KV" title="Club Brugge KV">Club Brugge</a> at Old Trafford, in which he scored a penalty, helping them to a 5–0 victory.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> On 16 March, Fernandes was voted as the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Player_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Player of the Month">Premier League Player of the Month</a> for February.<sup id="cite_ref-POTMFeb20_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POTMFeb20-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On 30 June, Fernandes scored his first brace for the club in a 3–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Brighton_%26_Hove_Albion_F.C." title="Brighton &amp; Hove Albion F.C.">Brighton &amp; Hove Albion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> For his performances in June, he won multiple club and Premier League awards, including Premier League Player of the Month and Goal of the Month, becoming the first player to win both awards concurrently in Premier League history.<sup id="cite_ref-POTMJun20_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POTMJun20-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GOTMJun20_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GOTMJun20-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> He also became the first Manchester United player to win back to back Premier League Player of the Month awards since <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_FA_Premier_League" title="2006–07 FA Premier League">2006–07 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> In September, Fernandes was named as the winner of Manchester United's <a href="/wiki/Sir_Matt_Busby_Player_of_the_Year" title="Sir Matt Busby Player of the Year">Sir Matt Busby Player of the Year</a> award, given to the club's best player from the previous season.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2020.E2.80.9321_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2020–21_season">2020–21 season</span></h4>
<p>On 26 September, Fernandes scored his first goal of the season against <a href="/wiki/Brighton_%26_Hove_Albion_F.C." title="Brighton &amp; Hove Albion F.C.">Brighton &amp; Hove Albion</a> in the 100th minute of a 3–2 win at the <a href="/wiki/Amex_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Amex Stadium">Amex Stadium</a>; it was one of the latest goals in Premier League history, and came after referee <a href="/wiki/Chris_Kavanagh_(referee)" title="Chris Kavanagh (referee)">Chris Kavanagh</a> had blown the final whistle, before a <a href="/wiki/Video_assistant_referee" title="Video assistant referee">video assistant referee</a> awarded United a penalty which Fernandes converted.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> On 7 November, Fernandes scored a brace and provided an assist against <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> to secure a 3–1 away win.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> He was named <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Player_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Player of the Month">Premier League Player of the Month</a> for November in recognition of his four goals and one assist that month.<sup id="cite_ref-POTMNov20_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POTMNov20-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and again in December after scoring three goals and providing four assists in that month, becoming the first player to win the award four times in a single calendar year.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> He scored one goal and made two assists in United's Premier League record-equalling <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C._9%E2%80%930_Southampton_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C. 9–0 Southampton F.C.">9–0</a> home win against <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a> on 2 February 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portugal_x_Alemanha_-_Futebol_masculino_-_Olimp%C3%ADadas_Rio_2016_(28342817733).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Portugal_x_Alemanha_-_Futebol_masculino_-_Olimp%C3%ADadas_Rio_2016_%2828342817733%29.jpg/220px-Portugal_x_Alemanha_-_Futebol_masculino_-_Olimp%C3%ADadas_Rio_2016_%2828342817733%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Portugal_x_Alemanha_-_Futebol_masculino_-_Olimp%C3%ADadas_Rio_2016_%2828342817733%29.jpg/330px-Portugal_x_Alemanha_-_Futebol_masculino_-_Olimp%C3%ADadas_Rio_2016_%2828342817733%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Portugal_x_Alemanha_-_Futebol_masculino_-_Olimp%C3%ADadas_Rio_2016_%2828342817733%29.jpg/440px-Portugal_x_Alemanha_-_Futebol_masculino_-_Olimp%C3%ADadas_Rio_2016_%2828342817733%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3713" data-file-height="2471" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portugal_x_Alemanha_-_Futebol_masculino_-_Olimp%C3%ADadas_Rio_2016_(28342817733).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fernandes playing for <a href="/wiki/Portugal_Olympic_football_team" title="Portugal Olympic football team">Portugal</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament" title="Football at the 2016 Summer Olympics – Men&#39;s tournament">2016 Summer Olympics</a></div></div></div>
<p>Fernandes has represented Portugal at five levels. Prior to his international debut, he was named <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captain</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_under-21_football_team" title="Portugal national under-21 football team">under-21 team</a> by coach <a href="/wiki/Rui_Jorge" title="Rui Jorge">Rui Jorge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Overlooked for selection by <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a> during his spell in Italy, Fernandes was first chosen on 28 August 2017, replacing the injured <a href="/wiki/Pizzi_(Portuguese_footballer)" title="Pizzi (Portuguese footballer)">Pizzi</a> for <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">World Cup qualifiers</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands_national_football_team" title="Faroe Islands national football team">Faroe Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hungary_national_football_team" title="Hungary national football team">Hungary</a> to be played the next month,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> although he did not play in either match.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Fernandes represented <a href="/wiki/Portugal_Olympic_football_team" title="Portugal Olympic football team">Portugal</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament" title="Football at the 2016 Summer Olympics – Men&#39;s tournament">2016 Summer Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> He started every game, as the team reached the quarter-finals.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Fernandes won his first full <a href="/wiki/Cap_(sport)" title="Cap (sport)">cap</a> on 10 November 2017, replacing <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Fernandes_(footballer,_born_1986)" title="Manuel Fernandes (footballer, born 1986)">Manuel Fernandes</a> for the last 34 minutes of the 3–0 <a href="/wiki/Friendly_(association_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Friendly (association football)">friendly</a> win over <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia_national_football_team" title="Saudi Arabia national football team">Saudi Arabia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Viseu" title="Viseu">Viseu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> He was then selected by <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Santos_(Portuguese_footballer)" title="Fernando Santos (Portuguese footballer)">Fernando Santos</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a> in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first goal on 7 June with a header in the last warm-up match before the tournament, a 3–0 defeat of <a href="/wiki/Algeria_national_football_team" title="Algeria national football team">Algeria</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_da_Luz" title="Estádio da Luz">Estádio da Luz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Fernandes' first World Cup game took place on 15 June 2018, when he played 66 minutes in a <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_B#Portugal_vs_Spain" title="2018 FIFA World Cup Group B">3–3 group stage</a> draw against <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a>, being <a href="/wiki/Penalty_card#Yellow_card" title="Penalty card">booked</a> in the process.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span></h2>
<p>An <a href="/wiki/Attacking_midfielder" class="mw-redirect" title="Attacking midfielder">attacking midfielder</a>, Fernandes is a direct, energetic <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Box-to-box_midfielder" title="Midfielder">box-to-box</a> <a href="/wiki/Playmaker" title="Playmaker">playmaker</a> who is capable of both taking on defenders and setting the rhythm of play.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Directness also means that Fernandes tends to take a lot of risks with the type and level of passes he attempts to complete, especially because he often tries to deliver killer ones. However, despite being prone to turnovers, he typically presses the opposition right after losing possession.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Fernandes boasts a prolific goalscoring record from the midfield position. He frequently shoots from outside the penalty area and is an accurate <a href="/wiki/Free_kick_(association_football)" title="Free kick (association football)">free-kick</a> taker.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> His movement off the ball is also key, with him often roaming around the attacking areas of the pitch, or dropping deep to pick up possession.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> As well as operating in the attacking midfielder role, he can also operate in a deeper <a href="/wiki/Central_midfielder" class="mw-redirect" title="Central midfielder">central midfield</a> role, or as a <a href="/wiki/Second_striker" class="mw-redirect" title="Second striker">second striker</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_68-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_2">Club</span></h3>
<p><b>Sporting CP</b>

<li>1976–77: <a href="/wiki/Stan_Bowles" title="Stan Bowles">Bowles</a></li>
<li>1977–78: <a href="/wiki/Gerrie_Deijkers" title="Gerrie Deijkers">Deijkers</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Raimondo_Ponte" title="Raimondo Ponte">Ponte</a></li>

<li>1979–80: <a href="/wiki/Dieter_Hoene%C3%9F" title="Dieter Hoeneß">Hoeneß</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Harald_Nickel" title="Harald Nickel">Nickel</a></li>
